Letter to the Editor 138

To the Editor,

I am writing in response to a report in your esteemed newspaper on the 5th of this month regarding the handover of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps First Regiment. The report stated that I dispatched Wang Chengzhi and Tong Xianglong, leading over a hundred men, to surround the regiment headquarters, oversee the regiment commander, and coerce the handover. It further alleged that I apologized to the regiment commander, which I found utterly astonishing upon reading.

Upon investigation, the reorganization of our army is a matter concerning the entire army, not merely the First Regiment. The authority to transfer officials rests with the committee and cannot be unilaterally exercised by any single individual. Furthermore, due to my limited abilities and the burden of other duties, I have already submitted my resignation to the committee. I did not even attend the meeting yesterday, so there is no basis for the alleged apology to the regiment commander.

The matter is entirely fabricated, and I fear that the public may be misled and confused, thereby distorting the truth. Therefore, I am writing this letter to clarify the situation and hope that you will publish it in your newspaper to shed light on the truth.

Sincerely,

Chen Ya-fu

December 5

Sixty-Four Athletes from Five Countries

Start at Eight O'Clock at the Intersection of Carter Road

The Entire Course is Seventeen Miles and One Hundred Yards

The 17th International Walking Race starts at 8:00 AM this morning at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Carter Road. Participants include 64 athletes from five countries: China, Britain, France, Russia, and Ireland. There are 44 individual participants. The course is seventeen miles and one hundred yards. The hope of China retaining the championship remains high.

The entire course is seventeen miles and one hundred yards, equivalent to over fifty Chinese li. There are markers along the way to prevent straying, and stations are set up every mile so that competitors can see their progress at a glance.

Jinan Fails in Senior Cup Competition and is Eliminated 147

Result: 1 to 2

Shanghai Team Wins with Ten Men

Jinan entered the Senior Cup competition for the first time yesterday, meeting the Shanghai team at the China Baseball Field. The game was intense. Despite the prestige of Jinan, the result was disappointing. They succumbed to the ten-man Shanghai team with a score of 1 to 2. The audience of over 4,000 spectators left disappointed. Referee: Lei Tu.

Shanghai Lineup

Xue Mingdeng, Jie Misen

Shi Duoke, Jin Bo

Kanaer, Boge Si, Hui Shimulun

Faping, Sinclair

Xue Wumolei

Jinan Lineup

Liang Shutang, Liu Zukan

Feng Yunyou, Qiu Dongyan

Wen Dingxin, Zhuang Shihong, Chen Zhenhe

Jiang Shanjing Shi Yang Baoshui, Chen Zhenxiang

Mei Hongbao

O Soul, Return!

The Jinan team, recognized as the pride of the football world, suffered a defeat to Lincoln the other day, reducing their hopes in the Group A competition. Yesterday, they suffered another setback, with their prospects in the Shanghai Senior Cup cut short. Has their football luck run out? Has their artistry deteriorated? Both seem to be the case. Considering yesterday's match, the Shanghai team has always been in the ranks of mediocre teams. Even if Jinan's victory could not be as easy as turning their hand, they should have been able to handle it with ease. However, the reality was contradictory, suffering a bitter defeat of 2 to 1. Moreover, it occurred during the absence of the famous Shanghai player Sinclair due to injury. Such a good opportunity yielded such a result, which is even more upsetting. Although victory and defeat are common occurrences, the Jinan athletes should gather their courage and strive to restore their reputation and demonstrate their great spirit, thereby grasping the leadership of Shanghai football. This failure may well be the mother of future success.

A Blessing in Disguise

Mr. Sinclair, the mainstay of the Shanghai team, left the field due to injury, causing turmoil throughout the team. The victory in fighting with ten men was unexpected. The strict defense and solid goalkeeper made it extremely difficult to break through. The loss of one goal and the result of the penalty kick was not their fault. There was not much activity from the forwards, but their style was quite fierce, and their shots were quite rare, but it was commendable that two actually hit the target. If Jinan had a reliable goalkeeper, at least one of the two goals could have been saved, and the Shanghai team would have been satisfied with a tie. How could they have achieved an excess of triumph?

Impending Disaster

The Shanghai team's ball progress was unsuccessful with several attacks. Liu Zukan was seen rushing in from the left wing, passing to the center. Chen Zhenhe took the opportunity to shoot twice, but both times failed to hit the target. Qiu Dongyan also added a shot, but it was still ineffective. Subsequently, Mei Hongbao picked out Liu Zukan, who headed the ball in front of the goal, creating a big wave. Jinan was unable to find a gap to enter the net. After thirty minutes, Qiu Dongyan kicked and injured Sinclair's leg, and he fell to the ground, and his injuries were serious. Spectators mostly criticized Qiu for his non-rule-following behavior. The Shanghai team suffered this major incident and had no time to attack, but worked hard on defense to avoid losses. Faping's two rescues were of great merit. The first half ended 0 to 0.

Good and Bad Turn Upside Down

The second half started. In less than two minutes, Qiu Dongyan scored a penalty kick. The ball hit the post and bounced in from the head of a defender. According to the Shanghai team's inner guard, the penalty kick was very unjust, because the ball hit his chest, not his arm. Jinan continued to occupy the field, but unfortunately could not penetrate deeply to break through the defenses. Once, Liu Zukan kicked a corner kick that landed in a critical position. Chen Zhenhe headed it out, and the ball flew towards the goal. The Shanghai goalkeeper jumped up and hit it out. Only someone with skill could have done this. The situation suddenly changed. Hui Shimulun kicked casually from 30 yards away. Goalkeeper Wen failed to catch it securely, and the ball rolled into the net. Shanghai tied the score 1 to 1, and their spirits were boosted. Soon, Mo Lei scored another goal. Jinan made efforts to counterattack. Under tense circumstances, the Shanghai goalkeeper snatched the ball and eliminated the danger. Finally, there was almost another penalty kick in the Shanghai penalty area, but because there was no evidence, it was changed to a throw. As a result, Shanghai won against Jinan 2 to 1 and advanced to the second week of the Senior Cup.

A Masterpiece by Sports Expert Wu Bangwei

In the midst of national crisis, devoting oneself to physical training is naturally a way to save the country. Free Talk

Memories of Dai Liang 152

— Yanzi

During the Jiawu Korean incident, relations between China and Japan deteriorated. In the battles of Incheon and Pyongyang, only Nie Shicheng's army fought valiantly against the Japanese army. However, the only one who was praised at the time was Zuo Baogui, who defended Pyongyang and died in a bloody battle. In fact, Nie's bravery and skill in battle were no less than Zuo's. After the incident was settled, Ye Zhichao and Wei Rugui were both convicted and imprisoned for the collapse of their armies. Li Hongzhang knew Nie's reliability well, and still relied on him, promoting him to the Governor of Zhili and leading the Wuwei Vanguard Army, alongside Dong Fuxiang, Yuan Shikai, and others, as a strong general in the new army. In the autumn of the Gengzi year, the Boxer Rebellion broke out in Tianjin. The Red Lantern women's corps were rampant for a time, and passersby looked sideways. The five ministers who were superstitious welcomed them with open arms. Dong Fuxiang, who led a large army, was especially devoted. Only Nie Shicheng's army remained unmoved. The Boxers who disturbed his defense area were wiped out without exception. The bandits hated him deeply, but there was nothing they could do. When the Eight-Nation Alliance invaded Tianjin, Nie led his troops to defend the key points. At that time, the vanguard of the Allied forces was the Japanese and German armies. Nie was not afraid of the powerful enemy and resisted valiantly, fighting in the Yangliuqing area. Nie's efforts allowed the two palaces to escape to the west. Seeing that Nie's army was resisting the enemy, the bandits secretly attacked from behind. Nie led his troops to divide their forces and engage in battle. Later, with exhausted ammunition and no reinforcements, the entire army was annihilated. Nie also died in battle with multiple bullets in his body. Those who heard it lamented. Alas, Nie Shicheng, as a warrior, was able to know the big picture, not be confused by the Boxer bandits, and not be subdued by the powerful enemy. He fought a bloody battle with a lone army and died for his country. Compared with Dong Fuxiang and others who did not know the order of things and left behind a stinking reputation, the difference cannot be measured. How magnificent is Nie Shicheng.

Do Not Remove the Grass in the Courtyard - A Big Talk Compilation

Dialogue Before the God of War (5) 153

"You say that if war breaks out, China will not necessarily be defeated. What basis do you have for saying that?"

"Japan cannot sustain a long war. Japan's domestic situation is also riddled with problems. Before the invasion of the Three Eastern Provinces, Japan's unemployment rate had already reached 1.5 million. Now, the unemployment rate is around 2.5 million. In Tokyo Prefecture alone, the number of impoverished people who lack adequate food and clothing exceeds 120,000. Thousands of homeless people sleep in the open in the Asakusa area at night. About 40% of university graduates specializing in professional fields cannot find jobs. Farmers nationwide are indebted to the tune of 500 million Japanese yen, which is equivalent to more than 1 billion Chinese dollars. Trade with China has fallen from first place to fifth place, and in the past two months or so, trade worth more than 150 million has been taken over by the United Kingdom and the United States. In this short period, nearly 300 million Japanese yen in cash has flowed to the United States. In the books "Anatomy of the Japanese Zaibatsu by Takahashi Kamekichi" and "The Theory of National Ruin by Joint-Stock Companies," we can see vivid pictures of the corruption and precarious activities of the Japanese financial world. Since the boycott of Japanese goods took effect, countless industrial organizations have collapsed. Due to convenient transportation and developed industries, the organization of the proletarian labor and agricultural classes is even more rigorous, and it has been progressing especially vigorously recently. Secret incitement is often discovered in the military. The Emperor is also not as sacred and inviolable as before. Slogans calling for the overthrow of the Emperor are commonly seen and heard. Japan's old forces are rushing towards collapse at an alarming rate. New forces are lurking everywhere, and they are constantly growing stronger, as if they are saying to the old forces, "He can be replaced by me!" All these circumstances do not allow Japan to sustain a long war. A long war will inevitably lead to the collapse of Japan's old forces. When the old forces are on the verge of collapse, they will not be able to fight again, and they will not dare to fight again."

"Japan is only unfavorable to a long war. What if they defeat our national army in one fell swoop? Wouldn't that be terrible?"

"The emergence of Ma Zhanshan in China has already made Japan unbearable. If war is formally declared, and the whole country is full of Ma Zhanshans, it will inevitably lead to a prolonged war. A long war will lead to the Japanese old forces being overthrown by the new forces without negotiating peace with us."

"After the Japanese old forces are overthrown, East Asia will have one more republic, and China will no longer be lonely."

"Whether Japan will establish a republic after the Japanese old forces are overthrown is still difficult to predict. However, declaring war on Japan will not only uphold justice for China but also provide great assistance to Japan's new forces. This can be asserted."

"If China's declaration of war on Japan helps Japan's new forces, then Japan's new forces should understand China's resistance."

"China's resistance will not only be understood by Japan's new forces, but also applauded and welcomed by all countries in the world that advocate justice and fairness, and they will all stand on our battle line. They are not applauding for us, but for justice and fairness. If we retreat from justice and fairness, then people of ambition all over the world will sigh for us, not sighing for us, but sighing for justice and fairness."

"Judging from this, the future seems quite optimistic."

"You cannot be too optimistic. Based on Chinese history, a Yue Wu Mu will emerge at this time, and there will also be a Qin Hui. At this moment, Yue Wu Mu is fighting against Qin Hui. Whether the Republic of China will become the second Song Dynasty depends on the outcome of the struggle between these two factions."

Ubiquitous Japanese Espionage Anecdotes 154

— Pinxia

Mr. Reggie Sheng is a native of Songjiang. In the past, he also served as a reporter for various famous Chinese-language newspapers in Shanghai. He often associated with Mr. Ma Jingniang, the Deputy Director-General and Acting Director-General of the British Municipal Council, and they discussed current affairs at length. One day, it happened to be a Sunday, and Mr. Ma specially ordered his servant to invite Mr. Sheng to his residence on Jing'an Temple Road for a conversation. Mr. Sheng immediately drove there. Upon arrival, Mr. Ma did not come out immediately. The servant said that the Director-General was currently taking a Japanese language lesson from a Japanese instructor and asked him to wait a moment. After a while, Mr. Ma finished the lesson and came out. Mr. Sheng smiled and asked, "The Director-General already masters six languages, including English, French, German, Russian, Italian, and Chinese. Does he still feel that it is not enough, so he is adding Japanese?" Mr. Ma said, "I have been studying Chinese for a long time, and I find Japanese very easy to learn. However, although Japanese is very easy to learn, the Japanese pronunciation cannot be mastered without being taught by a Japanese person." Mr. Sheng further inquired about how many months he had been studying Japanese on his own. He said, "It has been more than two months. I only spend one hour a day, but I think I have grasped the basics and it is enough to cope with things. As soon as the end of the month comes, I plan to dismiss the Japanese instructor." He also said, "There are many people like Sherlock Holmes among the Japanese. If I let him do this for a long time, I am afraid that many of my public and private secrets will inevitably be detected by him." Mr. Ma said to this point, and then said, "This reminds me of something. During the Boxer Rebellion in the Gengzi year, when the Boxers in Beijing besieged the embassies in the Eastern Legation Quarter, the ambassadors strictly ordered the military officers that no Chinese people outside the boundary were allowed to enter the embassy area. As a result, it was impossible for important figures in the embassies to find a barber. Later, they learned that there was only one Japanese barber in the area, so they reluctantly allowed him to serve them. He often went back and forth among the embassies. Later, when the Eight-Nation Alliance attacked Beijing from Tianjin, people in the embassies saw a person wearing a military uniform with shiny gold-edged epaulets and cap badges, riding a horse under the rising sun. He was the Japanese who had been cutting hair for people in the embassies. It was only then that they realized that the Japanese were doing this lowly job with hidden motives. They not only wanted to probe Chinese military intelligence but also wanted to spy on the secrets of the embassies. That is why I am deeply afraid of the Japanese."

Zhi Mo's Death (3) 157

— Liu Haisu

He used such enthusiasm, this fire-like passion, to encourage his friends. After reading this letter, anyone can clearly see the true Xu Zhimo. Because of his character, he became one of China's foremost new poets.

When I returned to China this time, I really wanted to meet Zhi Mo and reminisce about our long separation. Before I left Paris, I received a letter from him, knowing that he also had the same desire. He even wanted to wait for me in Shanghai.

The day after I arrived in Shanghai, at ten o'clock in the morning, I went to Zhi Mo's house on Foch Road. As soon as I entered the door, his servant said to me:

"Mr. Liu, you're back? The young master just went to Beiping yesterday."

I didn't say a word, feeling lost and disappointed. That night, I hastily wrote a letter to him at the Cangzhou Hotel, telling him that I had returned. How will you comfort me?

About six days later, I received a letter from him sent by airmail:

"Hai Su,

I estimate that you will arrive no later than the 15th. I postponed my departure to the 17th. You still haven't sent any news. I thought you must have been delayed in the south. As a result, I left and you arrived. The sorrow of separation for several years has not been expressed. I am extremely disappointed. After arriving here, I sent a letter to Xun Mei to ask if you had arrived, but I didn't receive a reply either. Last night, a letter arrived, which made me happy. Hai Weng's trip must be comparable to Xuanzang's trip to the Western Regions, bringing back many treasures. Living in the country for a long time has made me deaf and blind. I only hope that Hai Weng will return and we can talk freely. I didn't expect to miss each other again. My sister-in-law wants to come back together. What about the young master? The north is still calm. Can you come? Maybe I will want to go down once soon to see your masterpieces."

At that time, I was about to go to Nanjing, so I didn't write back to him. I returned to Shanghai from Nanjing about ten days later. Once, I heard at Zhi Mo's house that he was going to come south. After that, I waited for him every day.

On November 14th, I originally wanted to go to Hangzhou in the afternoon. Just as I was having lunch, Zhi Mo arrived. As he went up the stairs, he exclaimed loudly:

"Hai Su, Hai Tang, how are you? I've come to see your treasures."

I really couldn't describe the shock I felt in my whole body in that magical revelation of happiness. As the saying goes, "It is no regret to have one true friend in life." Zhi Mo was a true friend of mine for life, especially for my paintings.

He walked into the studio and carefully looked at my new works one by one. After looking at about twenty paintings, he sat on the sofa, his cheeks flushed with excitement, and said deeply:

"This is what painting is. It's satisfying to see. Hai Su, your power has reached beyond the canvas. You have established yourself, now you are... not just a Chinese person anymore. It's a pity that China talks about art like this. There are too few talents. But having one is enough..."

After that, he talked a lot about Paris, his face showing satisfaction and hope. He also talked about various things. I was just about to invite him to eat,

to invite him to eat. After eating, he would come back to look at the paintings in detail.

At about three o'clock, he used his naturally silver-like clear voice to shout upstairs, grabbing my hand and making me feel boundless warmth again.

to hold a Yanyihui to raise funds for the Shaanxi disaster relief. Mr. Chen also participated and performed on stage. It can be seen that he was enthusiastic about public welfare and did not only use this art for his own entertainment.

When Mr. Chen was in Shanghai, his residence was not far from mine, so I often visited him in my free time and had long talks. Mr. Chen had grand opinions on all aspects of academics, religion, current affairs, and so on. From this, it can be seen that Mr. Chen was not only proficient in art but also rich in thought.

This spring, when Mr. Chen took his family back to Chenzhou, he left a poem to bid farewell to his relatives and friends. The poem says, "Who is the first to awaken from the great dream? I am the first to wake up from the slumber. To seek a world of joy, I break the dream gourd. I have finished the karma of three lives, a string of Bodhi beads. I offer this cup to bid farewell, will there be another good meeting?" Everyone praised the poem for its transcendence. Who would have thought that it would become a prophecy?

It is said that when Mr. Chen was ill, Mr. Chen's elder brother became ill due to worrying about his younger brother's illness, and he could not recover. Mr. Chen's illness was so severe that his hands and feet were involved, and he also passed away. The two brothers, who went through thick and thin together, were comparable to Boyi and Shuqi on Shouyang Mountain.

Letter for correction: To the esteemed editor of "Free Talk" at Shen Bao. In the November 14th issue of your newspaper, Sun Choucheng's article "A Strange Tale of a Chaste Woman's Unrequited Love and Suicide" was published. After reading it, I am filled with pain. I, Lan, read some books in my childhood. Later, in the fifth year of the Republic of China, I married Zhang Zaifeng of Dongmuchang as my wife. I hoped to grow old together. Unexpectedly, my husband initially caught a cold the following year, but the pain turned into a serious illness. Medication was ineffective, and he passed away forever. Since my late husband's death, I have guarded his spirit tablet. Everyone in the neighborhood knows this. Now, Mr. Sun, without knowing the truth, recklessly submitted an article to the newspaper, claiming that a certain Shao was hired as a long-term worker and that they were having an affair, acting as master and servant by day and husband and wife by night. My family has never hired a long-term worker with the surname Shao. Moreover, my late husband's bones are not yet cold. Even in death, he is alive. How could I engage in indecent behavior? Furthermore, saying that I committed suicide due to unrequited love is even more laughable. I, Lan, am still alive in this world. Alas, Mr. Sun, your writing is profound, but I did not expect you to damage your own character, talk nonsense, and ruin the reputation of others. I would be extremely grateful if you could make a correction. With best wishes, Zhang Wang Lanzhen, November 22nd, from Hangzhou.

Securities and Bond Prices Plunge Together 163

Market Sentiment Weakens Due to Current Situation

Yesterday, at the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, the spot prices of all bonds, except for the 1929 National Loan at 96, opened sluggishly and trading remained quiet. In the futures market, prices also fell sharply. The January contract remained inactive, while the December contract saw slightly more trading than the previous day, with activity seen on both sides. However, the market trend indicated that selling was far more active than buying, causing bond prices to fall sharply due to oversupply. This was due to the government's decision not to agree to the neutral zone issue in accordance with public opinion, and the Japanese continued their unreasonable and barbaric conspiracies, leaving the future of diplomacy very bleak. Furthermore, the issue of peaceful reunification with Guangdong had not been fully resolved, causing renewed public unease and a surge in selling activity. However, investor confidence remained weak, and they remained on the sidelines. At the initial opening, prices fell sharply across the board, with further declines in subsequent trading. Later, the supply and demand gradually balanced, and prices fluctuated without significant changes. As a result, compared to the previous day, the 1919 Customs Bonds, 20th Year Consolidated Bonds (futures), and Troop Reduction Bonds (spot) all fell by three yuan. Other bonds fell by two to two and a half yuan. Only the Entire Sixth Salt Tax futures fell by about one yuan, and the 1926 Loan fell by only 75 cents. The future of the bond market remains as uncertain as before. It is estimated that the total futures trading volume was 6,395,000 yuan, with 4,550,000 yuan in the morning session and over 1,800,000 yuan in the afternoon session. The total spot trading volume was 48,000 yuan.

Cotton Yarn Market Also Declines 164

The yarn market is weak due to unfavorable news and tight credit conditions, leading to a lack of confidence. Those taking profits seize the opportunity to close positions, further weakening the market. Actual sales are particularly sluggish, and all traders lack active sentiment. The overall trend remains in a state of fluctuation.

Subject to Rumors, the Man Brand Yarn Market Opens Softly

The Man Brand Yarn market opened with a soft tone due to weak U.S. cotton prices. Prices for all months fell by 2, 4, 6, and 8 cents. In the afternoon, due to unfavorable rumors about national affairs, near-term contracts fell by 1 tael and 1 cent, and far-term contracts fell by 2 cents. The total trading volume for the day was 13,700 bales. Sales exceeded purchases by 1,800 bales, with Changji selling 1,600 bales and Changfeng selling 600 bales. Purchases were made by Dachangcheng (1,100 bales), Warui Da (600 bales), Xinchang (800 bales), and Tongyu (750 bales). The closing prices are listed below:

Spot Market Awaits Stability

Spot yarn sales are moderate. Total purchases by various traders for the day were 600 bales, with 165 bales traded among fellow merchants. The market is flat. Purchases by merchants from other regions included 300 bales for inland areas, 30 bales for Sichuan, 155 bales for Shantou, 10 bales for Tianjin, 70 bales for Guangdong, and 40 bales for miscellaneous regions.

Cotton Market Pressured by U.S. Cotton 165

The cotton market is flat and weak due to increasing private estimates of U.S. cotton yields, leading to softening sentiment. Gold prices are also weak, dragging down the market. However, Indian cotton prices are very high, and shipments from various regions remain scarce. Flower shops in rural areas report that sales are stagnant and credit conditions are tightening, leading to temporary closures and suspension of operations. Therefore, there is no prospect of vigorous sources of supply. However, the overall situation is very weak.

Hang Brand Yarn Market Declines

The Hang Brand Yarn market opened with a soft tone due to rising U.S. and Indian cotton prices. Prices for all months fell by 5 fen to 1.5 cents. In the afternoon, prices fell by another 5 fen to 1 cent. Total trading volume for the day was 50,300 dan. Sales were made by Gengfeng (6,400 dan), Yuchang (3,000 dan), and Changji (1,800 dan). Purchases were made by Yuanda (5,200 dan), Yifeng (2,200 dan), Xinheng (1,500 dan), and Yuchang (1,600 dan). The closing prices are listed below:

Divergent Trends in U.S., Indian, and British Cotton Prices 167

Yesterday, U.S. cotton prices weakened due to favorable harvest estimates for sellers and reduced buying on Wall Street. Futures fell by 6 to 8 points, and spot prices fell by 5 points. British cotton futures rose by 7 to 10 points, and spot prices rose by 9 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices rose by 5 points. Indian cotton was firm due to delayed arrival of Oomra cotton, leading to short covering. Phalgoor rose by 5.25 rupees, Oomra rose by 2.5 rupees, and White Rose rose by 3 rupees (original telegram).

U.S. Cotton Fluctuates Last Week 169

A New York telegram from the 4th reports on the cotton market over the past week: The cotton market was very quiet last week, with very narrow fluctuations. Cooperatives sold slightly during market rallies, and hedging in the South was very thin. There were also no signs of a loosening of hoarding activities. When prices fell, short covering and inter-dealer buying occurred. The overall trend seemed to be awaiting the government's estimate report or stabilization of the securities market. Bullish sentiment was largely based on the fact that prices were too low. However, the current situation still lacks certainty because the visible supply is too large and all industries show no signs of recovery. Although the Department of Agriculture opposed the export bonds or farmland relief fees advocated by agricultural leaders in the Senate Agriculture Committee, they may become law. Therefore, the final success or failure of this matter is still uncertain, resulting in a calm and unstable cotton market last week.

River Rice Market in Shanghai Falls by Half a Yuan 171

Yesterday, the supply from the countryside was still abundant, with over 50 dealers. Outbound sales in the city were extremely weak, and the situation collapsed. Chinese rice fell by half a yuan, and public sentiment stabilized. Merchants from the southern port purchased 500 shih of early and late rice. The local market had no appetite at all, so prices were uniformly lower by 2 jiao. Doyangjian rice arrivals were selling at a flat price, with no change. Transactions were sluggish. Breweries showed little interest, and prices were down by a few cents.

Around the Suzhou Creek in Xinzha, there were about 40 or 50 suppliers, but sales were stagnant. Xixin's medium-grade coarse rice was the most abundant, and prices fell by about 2 jiao. Shipments of thin rice from Shipu, Chonggu, Songjiang, etc. were also down by 2 or 3 jiao. Shipments of coarse rice and foreign rice were scarce, and the situation was stable. Although the arrival of glutinous rice was limited, demand was even weaker, and the overall price fell by a few cents.

Continued Transactions in Spot Foreign Rice 172

The rice market situation remained undeveloped yesterday, and the futures rice market seemed to be gradually sinking. However, there were still slight accommodations on the spot market from local merchants, and market prices remained flat. Although foreign firms showed intention to sell futures, there were no buyers interested, so there were no transactions in the overall market. Trading was also slow. Only the April contract for No. 1 Saigon rice traded 200 tons at a price of 5 taels. The Yinghua Company unloaded and offered a total of over 1,000 bags of No. 1 Saigon spot rice at a price of 11 yuan, 2 jiao, 3 fen to 11 yuan, 1 jiao, 5 fen. Taizhou's newly arrived rice was offered at 250 bags at a price of 10 yuan and 2 jiao, all of which were purchased by local merchants.

Sluggish Sales Lead to Weaker Wheat Flour Market 173

Yesterday, the wheat flour market trended weak. Although the quotations for foreign wheat only slightly declined, actual sales were sluggish. Large flour mills were already willing to lower prices below standard, and small and medium-sized mills naturally faced inventory accumulation. Therefore, public confidence in the current month weakened further. The opening price in the afternoon was 1 tael, 8 jiao, 7 fen, which was 2 and a half fen lower than the closing price of the previous day. Subsequently, buying from Tianjin traders slightly boosted sentiment, but the January contract was still being hedged. In this situation, there is no prospect of a good future. As a result, the current month was down by another 7 and a half li compared to the previous day, January was down 3 fen, February was down 1 fen, 2 li, 5 hao, March and April were down 1 fen, May was down 1 fen, 2 li, 5 hao.

Distant Wheat Market Extremely Weak 174

Yesterday, the futures wheat market showed a trend of near-term stability and distant-term weakness. In the current month, due to few sellers, a small number of millers slightly increased their purchases, causing the market sentiment to fluctuate. Distant-term months were reportedly contracted to be supplied with foreign wheat by mills from the western part of Hanzhou at a mere 3 taels, 8 jiao, 6 fen. With such a low price, distant-term wheat naturally could not stabilize, leading to a gradual decline and extreme weakness. As a result, the current month was up by 1 fen compared to the previous day, January was down 3 fen, February was flat, March was down 4 fen, and April was down 3 fen.

The Miscellaneous Grains Exchange has scheduled the opening of trading for December to begin on the 20th, and trading for distant-term months to continue until the 25th. The market will open on January 5th next year, as has been publicly announced.

Silk and Tea Factories Experience Continued Sluggish Sales 175

Yesterday, the silk market in Shanghai continued to be sluggish. White and yellow filature silk sales to Lyon remained stagnant. There were no transfers from New York. Stockpilers continued to try to suppress prices, and negotiations were proceeding. Of the 350 bales of white and yellow filature silk for which an agreement had been reached, there were still issues with the Chinese merchants, and only 40% of those contracts were actually signed and registered the day before yesterday. Yesterday, only Xinfu and others purchased 20 bales of yellow filature silk, and Xinshichang purchased 10 bales of dry white filature silk. Prices remained flat and weak.

Yellow and White Raw Silk Exports Increasingly Rare 176

The CCP only exported over 900 bales last month. European and American demand for dry white silk is insufficient. Last month (i.e., November), the CCP only shipped 111 bales to the United States, Britain, and France. Due to India's increased import duties, exports of coarse yellow silk from Sichuan, Shandong, and Hubei have also decreased. A total of only 793 bales were shipped out in November.

Foreign Tea Market Increasingly Quiet 177

Yesterday, the foreign tea market in Shanghai continued to be quiet. This was because British and French firms had exhausted their inventories of green tea from Tunxi, Shexian, and other areas. The only remaining tea on the market was the Wubei Zhenjie, which amounted to only 3,000 to 4,000 boxes. With current European sales underway, transactions were scarce. However, according to tea merchants, it should not be difficult to sell off all green tea inventories within the year.

Coal: Sales of Zhongmei Anthracite Slack 178

The Zhongxing brand of anthracite coal dust from Shandong province is one of the best domestic coals. It is used by various Chinese warships and railways. However, because of its high value, it is rarely used by factories and households. Recently, since the Wan'an Incident, factories have gradually purchased it, resulting in active sales. The price has gradually increased to over 15 taels per ton. Unexpectedly, due to the recent closure of various silk factories in both local and foreign areas, the outlet of various coal dusts has stagnated, and the sale of Zhongxing coal has also become sluggish. The selling price has also weakened. Yesterday, the market offered to sell it at 14 taels and a half per ton.

Shanghai Market

Market News 179

The Far East Longhua Lee Company, located at 46 Hankou Road, announces that the company is the manager of the famous French factory's fat, white, red-blooded beauty skin tablets, which supplement blood and nourish the skin. They are an essential product for European ladies to strengthen their bodies and beautify their skin. They were once shipped to Shanghai and sold out quickly. Now, another batch has arrived, which is still limited. Therefore, they will not be distributed to other cities for the time being. In Shanghai, the exclusive agent is Meili, located at 306 Nanjing Road, in the middle section of the British Concession. Detailed Chinese instructions are available upon request.

Medical Information 180

Dr. Gao Peiying, a female doctor located at the intersection of Guling Road and Changsha Road, has years of experience practicing at the Gengsheng Hospital in Suzhou and has extensive knowledge in obstetrics and pediatrics. Therefore, she has been very busy since opening her practice. She is providing free medical care for poor pregnant women.
